# Aurora — Core Completion Review

> A consolidation of what Aurora's reasoning core has proven in code, what it deliberately does not yet do, and the boundaries future work must not collapse.
>
> Review / Consolidation phase. No code, no production-module changes. This document summarizes; it does not decide.

| Field | Value |
|---|---|
| **Status** | Review / Consolidation · *Accepted snapshot* |
| **Phase** | Review (no implementation) |
| **Covers** | Implementations 001–006 (core) · **updated for 007 (Purpose `athlete`), 008 (projection freshness), 009 (AthleteDecision feedback), 010 (persistence ports + in-memory repositories), 011 (event/outcome records + traceability envelope), 012 (check-only reprojection harness), 013 (manual input adapter), 014 (deterministic rendering boundary), 015 (rendered-message record/review persistence), 016 (delivery boundary), 017 (provider adapter seam), 018 (provider-attempt audit), 019 (real-provider-ready boundary), 020 (concrete-provider adapter shell), 021 (opt-in live-provider boundary), 022 (injected environment credential resolver), 023 (one-file process-environment source adapter), 024 (ref-only provider/rendering/delivery occurrence event surface), 025 (explicit application orchestration boundary), 026 (opt-in live-provider smoke-test boundary), 027 (manual operator live-smoke entrypoint), 028 (provider-neutral managed-secret credential-source boundary), 029 (cloud-secret adapter contract behind the managed-secret seam), 032R-A (operator-mediated offline reflection runtime — Aurora's first product-runtime code slice, a pure application-level function `offlineReflectionRuntime(command, deps)` in `application-orchestration`), 035-A (pure Tier 2 external-renderable admission check — `admitExternalRenderable(request): ExternalRenderableAdmission` in `application-orchestration/application`), 035-B (admission check WIRED into `offlineReflectionRuntime` — runs after manual intake, before render-only orchestration; additive closed status `renderable-inadmissible`), 036-A (first operator-mediated reflection session — a TEST-ONLY whole-core responsible-reflection harness under `src/modules/__tests__/` proving the athlete-input-to-reflection loop end-to-end through the real chain; no production code)** |

no domain model, no repository, no persistence of its own — Impl 025 **— now also hosting Aurora's first PRODUCT-RUNTIME code slice: a pure application-level function `offlineReflectionRuntime(command, deps)` that wires the injected manual-intake collaborator (`deps.runManualIntake`) + the render-only `orchestrateRenderDeliver` to project a safe athlete-facing reflection, withhold delivery, and return a decision-capture prompt — operator-mediated offline/manual reflection only, NOT an executable script/package command/CLI/API/server/UI/worker/deployment target/production rollout/operator smoke; Impl 035-B**) — **and now also proven end-to-end by Aurora's FIRST operator-mediated reflection session as a TEST-ONLY whole-core responsible-reflection harness under `src/modules/__tests__/`** (a single new test file composing the real chain — athlete manual input → real `TerminalOutput` → `renderableFromTerminalOutput` → `RenderingRequest` → `offlineReflectionRuntime` → `admitExternalRenderable` (Tier 2) → render-only orchestration → downstream `validateDraft` → reflection-ready → delivery withheld → no `AthleteDecision`; AC20-permitted in `__tests__`, adding NO production code, NO whole-core composer, NO reflection-composition module; Impl 036-A**) — **plus one manual operator surface OUTSIDE `src`** (`scripts/operator-live-smoke.mjs` — a manual, executable, no-npm-script live-smoke entrypoint that wires real inputs into `liveProviderSmoke`; outside the default suite/CI; Impl 027) |

[FACT] **Central question:** *What exactly has Aurora's reasoning core proven in code, what does it intentionally not do yet, and what boundaries must future work not violate?*

---

## Update — Implementation 007 (Purpose-first `athlete`)

[FACT] Since this review was first written for Implementations 001–006, **Implementation 007** added a thin, **Purpose-first `athlete` module** — Aurora's first real *given* context. The body below has been corrected where it is affected; this banner is the at-a-glance summary of *what changed after Implementation 007*.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- `athlete` is an **implemented upstream module** (imports only `shared-kernel`; imports no `observation`/`reasoning`/`understanding`/`decision-support`).
- The implemented slice is **Purpose-only**: `Athlete` (thin root), `Purpose`/`DeclaredPurpose`, `PurposeVersion`, `PurposeVersionRef`, `PurposeHistory`, `PurposeChanged`, `PurposeChangeReason`, `PurposeSource`, `PurposeStatus`, `PurposeReinterpretationStatus` (type only), and a `RevealedPurposeSignal` placeholder.
- **`PurposeHistory` is append-only**; a change appends an immutable `PurposeVersion` and never overwrites the past.
- **`PurposeChanged` is a domain outcome/value** (returned/derived), **not** an event bus.
- **`PurposeVersionRef` can flow into `Hypothesis.purposeContextRef`** (the slot already existed — no reasoning refactor).
- **Purpose maps to decision-support `PurposeContext`** (missing→unknown, ambiguous→ambiguous, declared→declared) through a **neutral harness adapter**.
- **A purpose change can selectively stale understanding** via `markUnderstandingStale("purpose-change")` through a neutral harness adapter — `athlete` never mutates `UnderstandingProfile` directly and never resets it globally.
- **`Athlete` owns declared context, not inferred truth** — no state, capacity, readiness, fatigue, constraints, or path-dependent memory were implemented.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **thin Athlete/Purpose module ≠ full Athlete aggregate** — only the Purpose slice exists.
- **declared Purpose ≠ inferred athlete state** — `athlete` holds the *given*, never the *inferred*.
- **`PurposeChanged` ≠ reasoning rewrite** — prior hypotheses are never edited or auto-falsified.
- **`PurposeVersionRef` ≠ proof that old reasoning used the new purpose** — it is a context handle, tagging which purpose was in force; it does not retroactively re-evaluate.
- **Revealed behavior ≠ declared purpose** — only an athlete-sourced declaration creates a version; behavior never silently overwrites it.
- **Purpose context ≠ decision-support voice** — purpose feeds the `PurposeGate`; the case still selects the `VoiceMode`.
- **selective staleness ≠ global understanding reset** — only the named dimension(s) go stale.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora now has athlete-owned, versioned Purpose as real upstream context — but not a full Athlete model.** Purpose can constrain future reasoning and decision-support through explicit seams, while prior reasoning stays historically traceable and is never rewritten.

---

## Update — Implementation 008 (Projection Freshness on `UnderstandingAssessment`)

[FACT] **Implementation 008** made projection freshness **explicit** on `UnderstandingAssessment` (the one concrete projection today) and added a pure, selective refresh policy — all inside `understanding`, with **no `decision-support` change**.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- `UnderstandingAssessment` carries explicit **`freshness`** (`current`/`stale`/`partial`/`invalid`/`unknown`), **`derivedAt`**, **`sourceRefs`** (a `ProjectionTrace`), and **`limitations`** — all additive/optional, so 001–007 call sites are unchanged.
- New `understanding` surface: `ProjectionFreshness`/`Status`, `StalenessReason`, `ProjectionSourceRef`/`Kind`, `ProjectionTrace`, `ProjectionLimitations`, `RefreshTrigger`/`Kind`, `ProjectionRefreshDecision`/`Kind`, `ProjectionRefreshPolicy`, plus `clampCeilingByFreshness`/`applyFreshness`.
- **`current` preserves the Impl 006 Reflection scenario** byte-for-byte.
- **No non-current freshness can raise the voice;** `stale`/`partial` lower the ceiling one step; **`invalid`/`unknown` clamp `safeVoiceCeiling` to `none`** (→ `Withholding`).
- **`decision-support` was not modified** — freshness reaches it **only through the existing `safeVoiceCeiling`**; `understandingGate` still reads only the ceiling.
- **Refresh = recompute** (a new assessment); `applyFreshness` produces a **new** view and never mutates the old one; the prior assessment stays auditable if retained.
- The refresh policy is **pure, deterministic, selective** (only projections whose source refs intersect the trigger are affected), and **conservative** under uncertainty — it never globally invalidates and never invents traceability.
- **Still absent (intentional):** no generic projection engine, no top-level `projection` module, no persistence, no DB, no cache, no event bus, no UI/API/LLM, no `ImpactAssessment`.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **Projection ≠ source of truth** — `UnderstandingAssessment` is a derived read model of the `UnderstandingProfile` aggregate.
- **`ProjectionFreshness` ≠ traceability** — freshness says *how safe to consume*; trace/source refs say *what it came from*.
- **source refs ≠ copied source state** — references back to real artifacts, never embedded/re-authored truth.
- **refresh ≠ mutate old projection** — refresh recomputes a new view; the old one is never edited.
- **stale/partial/invalid/unknown ≠ permission to recommend** — non-current freshness can only constrain.
- **`safeVoiceCeiling` clamp ≠ decision-support owning freshness** — the consumer reads the (clamped) ceiling; it does not read freshness.
- **`UnderstandingAssessment` projection ≠ `UnderstandingProfile` aggregate** — the aggregate is the source of truth; the assessment is its labeled view.
- **local freshness slice ≠ generic projection engine** — freshness lives in `understanding` for one projection; no engine exists.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora now makes projection freshness explicit for `UnderstandingAssessment`; non-current freshness can only constrain downstream voice through `safeVoiceCeiling`, projections stay derived views, and there is still no generic projection engine or persistence.**

---

## Update — Implementation 009 (AthleteDecision Feedback Loop)

[FACT] **Implementation 009** closed the decision feedback loop: an athlete-owned, append-only `AthleteDecision` slice was added **inside `athlete`**, and a neutral harness adapter re-enters a reported decision as a `SubjectiveObservation` — **no `decision-support` / `observation` / `reasoning` / `understanding` change**.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- `AthleteDecision` is **implemented inside `athlete`** (athlete-owned, append-only); the `AthleteDecisionRef` placeholder is **retired** (it now references a real decision).
- New `athlete` surface: `AthleteDecisionId`, `AthleteDecision` (+ athlete-local `AthleteDecisionRef`, `DecisionReportSource`), `DecisionChoice`, `DecisionRationale`, `DecisionContext`, `DecisionOutcomeRef`, `AthleteDecisionRecord` (+ `amend`/supersede). Coordinators: `recordAthleteDecision`, `amendAthleteDecision`.
- **`DecisionSupportCase` records only an `AthleteDecisionRef`** — it references the decision, never owns or mutates it.
- The decision is **append-only**: corrections **amend/supersede**, the original stays auditable; `DecisionChoice` keeps a **modification** as free text (no binary compliance); `DecisionRationale` is athlete-reported context, not truth.
- **`DecisionOutcomeRef` is a reference only** — no full `DecisionOutcome` object; "no outcome" is the default.
- The decision **re-enters as a `SubjectiveObservation`** (via the neutral `__tests__` adapter, since `athlete` must not import `observation`) — an `Observation`, **never** `Signal`/`Evidence`/`Hypothesis`/`Understanding`. Future learning still passes the full ladder.
- **`divergedFromSupport` is neutral factual metadata**, not a compliance score; **good/bad outcome does not grade `SupportQuality`**.
- **Still absent (intentional):** no full `DecisionOutcome` object, no pattern engine, no compliance/obedience/shame/reward scoring, no outcome-based validation, no UI/API/DB/event-bus/persistence/LLM/training-plan.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **`AthleteDecision` ≠ Aurora output** — it is the athlete's fact, not Aurora's product.
- **`AthleteDecisionRef` ≠ ownership** — a reference recorded after the fact.
- **divergence ≠ noncompliance**, **following ≠ obedience-success**, **not-following ≠ failure** — no valence anywhere.
- **`DecisionOutcomeRef` ≠ outcome judgement** — a handle to a separate, later observation.
- **`AthleteDecision → Observation` ≠ `AthleteDecision → Evidence`** — re-entry is observation only.
- **`SupportQuality` ≠ outcome quality** — integrity at the time of support.
- **decision pattern ≠ athlete label** — a pattern must become a falsifiable hypothesis first.
- **decision rationale ≠ declared-purpose overwrite** — behavior never rewrites purpose.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **the athlete's decision now returns as athlete-owned learning material — referenced not owned, re-entering only as `Observation` through the ladder — with no obedience tracking, no shame, and no outcome-based grading of the support.**

---

## Update — Implementation 010 (Persistence Ports & In-Memory Repositories)

[FACT] **Implementation 010** added the first persistence slice: **repository ports + in-memory adapters** and an additive, validated **`toState()` / `reconstitute(state)`** surface per persisted boundary — proving round-trip safety with **no DB, ORM, schema, migrations, event bus, cache, or infrastructure**, and **no technology chosen**. All domain changes are **additive** (no behavior change; the prior tests stayed green).

[FACT] **Now true:**
- Persisted boundaries gained `toState()` (plain, serializable) + `static reconstitute(state)` (**validates invariants; rejects invalid state; rebuilds via existing constructors/helpers** — never a raw field bag): `ObservationSet`, `Hypothesis`, `UnderstandingProfile`, `DecisionSupportCase`, `Athlete`, `AthleteDecisionRecord`.
- Each has a **module-owned repository port** (`save`/`findById`/`exists`) and an **in-memory adapter** (module-local `application/`, **not** infrastructure). `AthleteDecisionRecord` is keyed by `athleteRef`; **`PurposeHistory` persists *through* `Athlete`**.
- In-memory repositories **store state copies, not live references** (deep-copy via `structuredClone` on save *and* load), so **two finds return independent objects** and **mutating a retrieved object never touches the store** (mutation isolation proven).
- **Round-trip preserves**: identity, provenance, **append-only history**, **supersession**, **traceability refs**, terminal output + support integrity, and **`AthleteDecisionRef` (referenced, not owned)**.
- **Projection freshness survival** is proven via an **in-memory test helper** — there is **no projection repository**; a stored assessment loads still as a labeled view (invalid/unknown → ceiling `none`).
- **Still absent (intentional):** no production DB/ORM/schema/migrations, no event bus, no cache, no `src/infrastructure`, no `persistence`/`repositories` module, no projection repository, no event records.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **persistence ports ≠ production database** · **in-memory repository ≠ infrastructure layer**.
- **`toState()` ≠ domain authority** · **`reconstitute(state)` ≠ a raw field-bag bypass** (it validates).
- **persisted state ≠ current truth** · **repository round-trip ≠ event sourcing**.
- **traceability refs ≠ database foreign keys** · **projection-freshness survival helper ≠ projection repository**.
- **`DecisionSupportCase` repository ≠ `AthleteDecision` ownership** · **a state copy ≠ a live domain-object reference**.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora can now save and reload its aggregates and stateful records through validated ports + in-memory adapters without corrupting invariants, traceability, freshness, append-only history, or ownership — while production persistence, event records, and all infrastructure remain intentionally absent.**

---

## Update — Implementation 011 (Domain Event/Outcome Records & Traceability Envelope)

[FACT] **Implementation 011** added a new **dependency-neutral `event-recording` module** that records *what happened* as an **append-only, ref-only** log — turning the persistence paper's §4 event surface from conceptual into code, while staying **non-command, non-bus, non-infrastructure**. It is **additive**: the only existing-file change is a documented one-line test allowlist for the new module directory; **no production module was modified**.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- A new module `src/modules/event-recording/` exists and **imports only `shared-kernel`**; **no domain module imports it**; the **event catalog lives outside `shared-kernel`** (the kernel never becomes event-aware).
- **One `DomainEventRecord`** carries two categories — **`occurrence`** (something was observed/created) and **`outcome`** (the result of an operation) — over a **closed 26-type catalog** (`DOMAIN_EVENT_TYPE`); there is **no parallel `DomainOutcomeRecord` class**.
- A record carries: id, type, category, `occurredAt`, `recordedAt`, producing module, a **`TraceabilityEnvelope`** (primary artifact ref + source refs + typed slots + optional projection-freshness *status label* + limitations), **ref-only `EventPayloadRef[]`**, and optional `EventActor` / `CausationRef` / `CorrelationRef`.
- **Payloads are ref-only by construction** — `EventPayloadRef` carries only `kind`/`id`/`role?`/`ownerModule?`; **copied aggregate state and arbitrary `metadata`/`payload` bags are unrepresentable**, and reconstitution rejects smuggled extra keys.
- **Records are append-only** — `DomainEventRecordLog` is immutable-by-operation (`append` returns a new log; duplicate ids rejected; order preserved); corrections/supersessions are **new records**. The **in-memory repository stores copies, not live references** (deep-copy on append/find/all) and exposes **no** `update`/`delete`/`dispatch`/`publish`/`subscribe`/`markProcessed`.
- **Catalog-driven validation** runs on both construction *and* `reconstitute(state)`: type↔module, type↔category, required primary-ref kind, required refs, required freshness marker, required output-kind role, required athlete actor, and `occurredAt ≤ recordedAt`. Reconstitution **re-validates and rejects invalid state**, executes nothing, and changes no timestamp.
- **Causation = lineage, correlation = grouping** — neither forms an execution chain; appending a record triggers no downstream mutation.
- **Still absent (intentional):** no event bus, no publish/subscribe, no handlers, no async delivery, no DB/schema/serialization tech, no `src/infrastructure`, no event sourcing, no projection engine, no production event store.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **event record ≠ command** · **event record ≠ aggregate** · **event record ≠ projection** · **event record ≠ source truth**.
- **event record ≠ event-bus message** · **event log ≠ event sourcing** (it records occurrences; it does not rebuild aggregates — `reconstitute` does).
- **correlation ≠ command chain** · **causation ≠ handler trigger**.
- **payload ref ≠ copied state** · **traceability envelope ≠ database foreign key**.
- **`DomainEventRecordRepository` ≠ production event store** · **occurrence/outcome record ≠ downstream mutation**.
- **`TerminalOutputSelected` event ≠ `AthleteDecision`** · **`AthleteDecisionRecorded` event ≠ compliance score** · **`ProjectionFreshnessChanged` event ≠ projection made current by assertion**.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora now records *what happened* in an append-only, ref-only, traceable log — complementing the aggregate repositories (which answer *what is the aggregate now?*) without replacing them, and without becoming a command, copied state, a projection, source truth, a bus, or event sourcing.**

---

## Update — Implementation 012 (Check-Only Reprojection Harness)

[FACT] **Implementation 012** added a **neutral, check-only reprojection harness** — a recompute-and-compare *safety mechanism* that re-derives derived views, recalculates freshness, verifies traceability, detects candidates from event records, and **reports** drift/findings. It is **test-support / coordination seam, not production architecture**: it lives under `src/modules/__tests__/reprojection-harness/`, **no production `reprojection` module exists**, and **no existing module was modified**.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- A check-only harness (`runReprojection`) exists under `src/modules/__tests__/reprojection-harness/` — composed of `ReprojectionRun`/`Result`/`Finding`/`Mode`/`Target`/`InputSet`, a pure event→candidate map, and an `understanding` recompute adapter.
- It **recomputes `UnderstandingAssessment`** *through the owning module's existing function* (`produceUnderstandingAssessment` + `applyFreshness` + the Impl 008 freshness helpers) — the harness **coordinates, it does not reason**; it never derives a level or applies a transition.
- It **recalculates the 5-state freshness** (and may only re-derive the **same or a more cautious** view — never promotes freshness, never raises a ceiling).
- It **detects candidate targets from `DomainEventRecord`s** via a **pure** map (`PurposeChanged`→stale, `ObservationSuperseded`→invalid/source-superseded, hypothesis events→`requires-policy-transition`, etc.) — events **identify what to check**, they **execute nothing**.
- It **reports drift** (`changed` + a differences summary) instead of overwriting; **reports** `missing-traceability`/`stale`/`invalid`/`requires-policy-transition`/`manual-review-required`; and attaches a diagnostic `SafeActionCategory` (never athlete-facing).
- **`check-only` is the default and only implemented mode**; `refresh-derived`/`mark-stale` are **reserved and throw**. A run **mutates no repository, appends no event record, creates no decision-support output, and calls no write method** (proven by a before/after deep-equality snapshot and a throwing-`save` that is never reached).
- **Empty repositories are never rebuilt from the event log** — an event referencing an absent aggregate yields `event-record-only`/`missing-source`, never synthesized state.
- **Still absent (intentional):** no production `reprojection` module, no scheduler, no event bus, no event sourcing, no projection repository, no production service/orchestration layer.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **reprojection harness ≠ production service** · **check-only ≠ a write path** · **reprojection ≠ event sourcing**.
- **event records ≠ aggregate-rebuild commands** · **events-as-candidates ≠ event execution** · **repository state ≠ event log**.
- **recomputed projection ≠ source truth** · **drift report ≠ overwrite** · **freshness recalculation ≠ freshness promotion**.
- **stale/invalid finding ≠ recommendation** · **DecisionSupport review finding ≠ `TerminalOutput`** · **`AthleteDecision` outcome ≠ `SupportQuality` rewrite** · **purpose-related stale finding ≠ `Purpose` overwrite** · **reserved mode ≠ implemented mode**.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora can now recompute and verify its derived views — recalculating freshness, identifying candidates from occurrence history, and reporting drift — while provably mutating no aggregate, executing no event, rebuilding nothing from the log, and turning no projection into truth; and it does so as a neutral check-only harness, not production architecture.**

---

## Update — Implementation 013 (Manual Input Adapter)

[FACT] **Implementation 013** added Aurora's first **real "data in" boundary**: an **`observation`-owned Manual Input Adapter** that records manually supplied athlete/training information faithfully as an `ObservationSet` — and refuses what it cannot represent. It records *source material*, never *meaning*. It is **additive**: `observation/index.ts` gained exports only (no behavior change); the one other change is a documented test-only guard-precision fix.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- `src/modules/observation/application/manual-input-*` implements `ManualInputSubmission`, `ManualInputEntry` (closed union), `ManualInputIngestionOutcome` (`accepted`/`partially-accepted`/`rejected`), closed **rejection/limitation/quality** catalogs, and **`ingestManualInput({ submission, observationSetRepository })`**.
- The adapter's **only domain output is an `ObservationSet`** — built via the existing **`recordObservationSet`** and persisted **only** through **`ObservationSetRepository`** (no bypass, no DB).
- It preserves **verbatim subjective `words`**, records **explicit missing data** (never invents values), and preserves **provenance/quality** with **`source: "manual"`** (the reporter is preserved in the provenance reference).
- **Rejection saves nothing** (a throwing `save` is never reached); **partial acceptance** records only the faithful entries and reports limitations for the rest; ambiguity becomes a limitation or a rejection, never an inference.
- `measured-value` is **reserved** (no unit interpretation yet → limitation/rejection); `athlete-decision-report` is recorded **only as a subjective/context observation** — **no `AthleteDecisionRecord` mutation**, no compliance score.
- The adapter **imports no downstream module** (`reasoning`/`understanding`/`decision-support`/`athlete`) and **no `event-recording`**; **`observation` stays `event-recording`-free**. An optional `ObservationSetRecorded` is composed **only in a neutral harness** from a **ref-only** event candidate, and is inert.
- **Still absent (intentional):** no UI, API, LLM, external/FIT/wearable integration, DB/schema, event bus, scheduler.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **manual input ≠ meaning** · **adapter ≠ reasoning** · **saved `ObservationSet` ≠ `Signal` detection**.
- **subjective words ≠ inferred fatigue/readiness** · **missing data ≠ invented value** · **partial acceptance ≠ silent interpretation** · **rejection ≠ accidental data loss**.
- **source quality ≠ athlete quality** · **event candidate ≠ event command** · **`ObservationSetRecorded` ≠ downstream execution**.
- **athlete-decision report as observation ≠ `AthleteDecisionRecord` mutation** · **Manual Input Adapter ≠ UI/API/LLM/external integration**.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora now accepts manually supplied input as faithful `ObservationSet`s — preserving provenance/source/quality and verbatim words, representing missing data explicitly, rejecting the unrepresentable, and persisting through the repository port — without interpreting input, detecting signals, reasoning, mutating athlete records, or triggering any downstream effect; the adapter is a scribe, not an interpreter.**

---

## Update — Implementation 014 (Deterministic LLM Rendering Boundary)

[FACT] **Implementation 014** added Aurora's first **"output out"** boundary: a downstream **`rendering` module** that turns a domain-approved `TerminalOutput` into human-facing text — preserving the domain's voice, uncertainty, limitations, freshness, traceability, and agency. The renderer **expresses**; it never **decides, escalates voice, strengthens a claim, hides uncertainty, invents a fact, or becomes authority**. It is **additive**: the only existing-file change is the documented `ALLOWED_MODULES` allowlist update for the new module.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- A new module `src/modules/rendering/` exists: `RenderableDomainOutput` (+ module-local `RenderableFreshness`), `RenderingRequest` (+ closed `SAFE_STYLES`/`SUPPORTED_LOCALES`), `RenderedMessage`/`RenderOutcome`, a closed **12-value `RenderingFailure`** catalog, the `RenderingPolicy` cue vocabularies, a **mandatory `RenderingValidator`**, a deterministic **fake renderer**, and `renderableFromTerminalOutput`.
- **Rendering is downstream presentation, not reasoning and not `decision-support`.** `decision-support` owns the `TerminalOutput` and `VoiceMode`; the renderer reads a **read-only projection** and owns **phrasing only**.
- The **fake renderer is deterministic** (no provider, no model, no randomness; same request → same text); **every draft passes the mandatory validator** before becoming a `RenderedMessage`. **The validator, not the renderer, is the safety guarantee.**
- The validator (structural/string-based) **rejects**: voice escalation, recommendation language where not domain-approved, inquiry-rendered-as-answer, withholding-rendered-as-advice, hidden uncertainty, hidden limitations, missing/invented traceability (completeness claims over an incomplete chain), invented facts, unsupported style/locale, and unsafe athlete-state/purpose/compliance/event-command language — and any failure **degrades to safe non-rendering**.
- **Voice may match or soften, never escalate**; `Inquiry` stays a question; `Withholding` stays a refusal; `Recommendation` preserves conditions, uncertainty, traceability, and agency.
- A `RenderedMessage` is **not domain authority** — not `Evidence`/`Observation`/`Understanding`/`AthleteDecision`, not source truth; rendering **mutates no aggregate**, **writes no event**, and **persists nothing**.
- `rendering` **imports only `shared-kernel` + read-only `decision-support` types**; **no existing domain module imports `rendering`**; **no real LLM provider / prompt templates / UI / API / external call** exists.
- **Still absent (intentional):** a real LLM provider, prompt templates as production code, UI/API/external delivery, rendered-message persistence, and rendered-output event records.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **rendering ≠ reasoning** · **generated text ≠ domain authority** · **renderer ≠ voice selector** · **`VoiceMode` ≠ style request**.
- **fake renderer ≠ LLM provider** · **validator ≠ model quality** · **renderable output ≠ raw reasoning internals**.
- **rendered message ≠ `Evidence`/`Observation`/`Understanding`/`AthleteDecision`** · **rendering failure ≠ unsafe fallback**.
- **style request ≠ permission to escalate voice** · **Recommendation rendering ≠ recommendation creation** · **Withholding rendering ≠ advice** · **Inquiry rendering ≠ answer** · **traceability summary ≠ invented citation**.
- **rendered-text persistence ≠ implemented** · **event record for a rendered message ≠ implemented**.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora can now express a domain-approved terminal output in human-facing language — deterministically, behind a mandatory validator — while the generated text never selects voice, strengthens a claim, hides uncertainty, invents a fact, mutates state, or becomes authority; rendering expresses the domain's decision, it never makes one.**

---

## Update — Implementation 015 (Rendered-Message Record / Review Persistence)

[FACT] **Implementation 015** closed the first **auditable output-out cycle**: a **rendered-message record + display-safety review**, kept **inside `rendering`** (not a new module). It records and reviews presentation artifacts **without** turning generated text into domain truth or review approval into reasoning. It is **additive**: only the two `rendering` index files changed (additive exports); **no new top-level module**, **no documented blocker**.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- `rendering` gained (in `domain/` + `application/`): `RenderedMessageRecordId`/`RenderReviewId`, `RenderedMessageRecord` (+ `RenderedMessageRecordState`), `RenderReview` + closed `RenderReviewDecision` (5) / `RenderReviewReason` (11) / `ReviewerKind`, `DisplayEligibility` + `displayEligibilityOf`, and a `RenderedMessageRecordRepository` **port** + `InMemoryRenderedMessageRecordRepository`.
- A `RenderedMessageRecord` is an **append-only, auditable presentation artifact** that **preserves the source domain output ref**, terminal output kind, `VoiceMode` at render time, text (if rendered), validation/preservation flags, renderer kind, and `createdAt`. **It is not domain authority** (not `Evidence`/`Observation`/`Understanding`/`DecisionSupport`/`AthleteDecision`/source truth).
- **Review history is append-only**; **current review status is derived** from the latest entry (`not-reviewed` initially; `superseded` from `supersededBy`). **Display eligibility is derived** (rendered + `approved-for-display` + not superseded + source ref + preservation flags intact) — and **display eligibility is not delivery, not domain approval, not recommendation creation; it triggers nothing**.
- **Approval changes no domain** — not `VoiceMode`, confidence, traceability, freshness/limitations, or `SupportQuality`; **rejection invalidates nothing** upstream; **revision/supersession preserve** the old record (immutable; no silent overwrite); a **failed attempt** is auditable but **never display-eligible and cannot be approved**.
- The **repository** uses the Impl 010 pattern (deep-copy `toState()`↔`reconstitute()`; **mutation isolation**; **invalid state rejected**); **no production DB/schema/ORM/migration**.
- **No rendered-output events**: a `RenderedMessageRecord` is **not an event record**; **`rendering` imports no `event-recording`** and the **event catalog is not expanded**. **No delivery / UI / API / provider / prompt templates.**

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **rendered-message persistence ≠ domain authority** · **review approval ≠ stronger evidence** · **display eligibility ≠ delivery** · **presentation review ≠ reasoning review**.
- **persisted rendered text ≠ `Observation`/`Evidence`/`Understanding`/`DecisionSupport`/`AthleteDecision`** · **source ref preservation ≠ source-truth conversion**.
- **review rejection ≠ domain invalidation** · **revision ≠ overwrite** · **supersession ≠ deletion** · **failed render audit ≠ displayable message**.
- **repository persistence ≠ production DB** · **rendered-message record ≠ event record** · **no rendered-output event ≠ missing auditability**.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora can now conserve and review rendered text as an auditable presentation artifact — append-only records, append-only review, derived display eligibility — improving auditability and display safety only, never making the text domain truth, mutating the domain, repairing traceability, emitting an event, or triggering delivery.**

---

## Update — Implementation 016 (Delivery Boundary)

[FACT] **Implementation 016** added the first **delivery / exposure** boundary: a **new downstream `delivery` module** that exposes a *display-eligible* `RenderedMessageRecord` to a target and records the attempt as an auditable `DeliveryRecord`. Delivery is **downstream exposure**, not rendering and not domain — it **verifies** eligibility, it never decides, interprets, or reinterprets. It is **additive**: two **documented test-only** blocker fixes landed (the e2e `ALLOWED_MODULES` set gained `delivery`; the Impl 015 forbidden-layer test dropped its obsolete `delivery` entry); **no production module was modified**.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- A new module `src/modules/delivery/` exists, importing **only `shared-kernel` + read-only `rendering`** types/functions; it imports **no** `observation`/`reasoning`/`understanding`/`decision-support`/`athlete`/`event-recording`; **`rendering` does not import `delivery`**; **no upstream module imports `delivery`**.
- `domain/` implements: ids (`DeliveryRequestId`/`DeliveryRecordId`), the closed **`DeliveryTarget`** (only `test-sink` supported; `manual-review-surface`/`future-ui`/`future-notification-channel` reserved), the closed **`DeliveryOutcome`** (`accepted-for-delivery` [reserved] / `blocked-not-eligible` / `delivered` / `failed` / `cancelled` / `not-attempted`), the closed **`DeliveryFailureReason`** (10 reasons; `provider-unavailable` **excluded**, `sink-unavailable` added), `DeliveryRequest`, `DeliveryEligibilityCheck` (+ the raw-reason→failure-reason mapping), the `DeliverySink` interface + deterministic **`InMemoryTestSink`**, and the auditable `DeliveryRecord` (+ `DeliveryRecordState`, validated `toState`/`reconstitute`).
- `application/` implements the **`DeliveryRecordRepository` port** + `InMemoryDeliveryRecordRepository` (deep-copy round-trip, mutation isolation, validated reconstitution, `findByRenderedMessageRecordRef`) + the **`requestDelivery`** service (the only file importing `rendering`).
- **Eligibility is reused, not reinterpreted:** `requestDelivery` calls `rendering`'s **`displayEligibilityOf(record)`** and maps its specific reasons to a specific `DeliveryFailureReason` (raw reasons retained). The deterministic sink is called **only** when the record is eligible *and* the target is the supported `test-sink`; **not-reviewed / rejected / superseded / failed-render / missing-ref** records and **unsupported/reserved targets** are **blocked** without calling the sink.
- **Delivery is auditability, not authority:** a `DeliveryRecord` is **not** source truth / `Evidence` / `Observation` / `Understanding` / `DecisionSupport` / `AthleteDecision`; **delivery success is not evidence** and **delivery failure is not domain invalidation**; delivery **mutates no rendered-message record and no aggregate**, **triggers no reasoning/reprojection/retry**, and **emits no event**.
- **Still absent (intentional):** no real provider/channel (email/SMS/push/WhatsApp/web), no UI/API, no scheduler/retry/background-job layer, no event bus, no **delivery event records**, no event-catalog expansion, no production DB/schema/ORM/migration.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **delivery ≠ rendering** · **delivery ≠ domain reasoning** · **display eligibility ≠ delivery**.
- **delivery verifies `displayEligibilityOf` ≠ delivery re-derives eligibility** — verify, never reinterpret.
- **`DeliveryRecord` ≠ `Evidence`/`Observation`/`Understanding`/`AthleteDecision`/`DecisionSupport`** · **delivery success ≠ support validation** · **delivery failure ≠ domain invalidation**.
- **`test-sink` ≠ real provider/channel** · **`InMemoryTestSink` ≠ email/SMS/push/WhatsApp/UI/API**.
- **delivery audit ≠ event record** · **delivery repository ≠ production DB** · **no delivery event ≠ missing auditability**.
- **accepted/delivered outcome ≠ athlete outcome** · **delivered text ≠ source truth** · **retry/scheduler ≠ implemented** · **`accepted-for-delivery` ≠ produced this slice (reserved)**.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora can now expose a reviewed, display-eligible rendered message to a deterministic test sink and record the attempt as an auditable `DeliveryRecord` — exposure and auditability only, never authority: it verifies (not re-derives) eligibility, blocks everything ineligible, and lets neither delivery success nor failure touch the domain, become evidence, or trigger reasoning; and it does so behind a closed boundary with no real channel/provider, UI/API, scheduler, event, or DB.**

---

## Update — Implementation 017 (Provider Adapter Seam)

[FACT] **Implementation 017** added the most dangerous output-out boundary safely: a **provider adapter seam inside `rendering`** that lets a future LLM provider **draft** human-facing text — as an **untrusted draft** that becomes a `RenderedMessage` **only** by passing the **unchanged mandatory `validateDraft`**. The provider replaces **only** the draft-text step the `FakeRenderer` performs; the validator, not the provider, remains the authority. It is **additive**: only the two `rendering` index files changed (additive exports); **no new top-level module**, **no documented blocker**.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- `rendering` gained (in `domain/` + `application/`): a constrained **`ProviderRenderingRequest`** (+ the `providerRenderingRequestFrom` construction guard), an untrusted **`ProviderDraft`**/`ProviderDraftOutcome`, a closed **`ProviderFailure`** catalog (10 values), a **`ProviderAdapter`** port, a deterministic **`FakeProviderAdapter`** (safe + each unsafe scenario + each failure), and a **`requestProviderRendering`** service returning a thin **`ProviderRenderOutcome`** around the existing `RenderOutcome`.
- The mandatory flow is **provider produces draft → `validateDraft({ draft, renderable, request })` → `RenderedMessage` only if validation passes**. The `rendered` branch's `message` is **exactly** the existing rendering path; a validation failure → **`provider-output-failed-validation`** with the underlying `RenderingFailure[]`.
- The **`ProviderRenderingRequest` is a constrained projection** of the authoritative `RenderingRequest` — only domain-approved fields (kind, domain-selected `VoiceMode`, allowed/forbidden claims, uncertainty/limitation requirements, traceability constraints, safe style/locale). It carries **no** raw private reasoning, chain-of-thought, mutable aggregate handle, override-voice/hide-uncertainty/ignore-validation field, arbitrary prompt text, or provider payload — those are **unrepresentable**.
- An **unsafe request is refused before any provider call** (`unsupported-style`/`unsupported-locale`/`unsafe-provider-request`); a provider failure maps to a closed reason (the network-flavored `provider-unavailable`/`-timeout`/`-rate-limited` are **fake-configurable**, no real semantics); **every** failure path **degrades to safe non-rendering**.
- A **`ProviderDraft` is untrusted** — it is **not** a `RenderedMessage`/`RenderedMessageRecord`/`Evidence`/`Observation`/`Understanding`/`AthleteDecision`/`DecisionSupport`; the provider **cannot** construct a `RenderedMessage` directly, **selects/changes no `VoiceMode`**, **creates no `TerminalOutput`/`Recommendation`**, and **persists/reviews/marks-display-eligible/delivers/emits-an-event/mutates nothing**.
- The seam **imports only its own `rendering` surfaces + read-only `decision-support` types**; **no module outside `rendering` imports it**; there is **no real provider SDK/API/network/`process.env`/prompt-templates-as-code** and **no `provider`/`llm`/`openai`/`anthropic`/`model` top-level module**.
- **Still absent (intentional):** a real provider/SDK + production prompts; provider-attempt persistence; provider event records; UI/API; a scheduler/retry layer; a production DB.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **provider draft ≠ rendered message** · **provider adapter ≠ renderer authority** · **provider draft ≠ domain truth**.
- **provider draft ≠ `TerminalOutput`/`Recommendation`/`Evidence`/`Observation`/`Understanding`/`AthleteDecision`** · **provider draft ≠ rendered-message record**.
- **provider success ≠ display eligibility** · **provider success ≠ delivery** · **provider failure ≠ domain invalidation** · **validation failure ≠ review rejection**.
- **fake provider ≠ real provider integration** · **provider seam ≠ SDK/API/network/prompt implementation** · **provider request ≠ raw private reasoning**.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora can now let a (fake, deterministic) provider draft rendered text behind the unchanged mandatory validator — the provider is only an untrusted draft source: it can never select voice, create a claim/terminal-output/message/record, bypass validation, persist/review/deliver, emit an event, or mutate the domain; an unsafe request is refused before the call and every failure degrades to safe non-rendering; and no real SDK/API/network/prompt or provider module exists.**

---

## Update — Implementation 018 (Provider Attempt Audit)

[FACT] **Implementation 018** added the last safety belt before a real provider: a **provider-attempt audit inside `rendering`** that records *what the seam did* — **auditability, not authority** — **without retaining raw drafts** or letting an attempt become source truth, evidence, or reasoning. It is **additive**: only the two `rendering` index files changed (additive exports); **no new top-level module**, **no documented blocker**.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- `rendering` gained (in `domain/` + `application/`): `ProviderAttemptRecordId`, **`ProviderAttemptStatus`** (closed; `requested`/`draft-produced` reserved), **`ProviderAttemptFailureReason`** (= `ProviderFailure | RenderingFailure`, real catalogs reused verbatim), **`ProviderDraftSummary`** (safe, no raw text), **`ProviderAttemptRecord`** (+ `ProviderAttemptRecordState`), a **`ProviderAttemptRecordRepository` port** + `InMemoryProviderAttemptRecordRepository`, and the observe-only **`auditProviderAttempt`** service.
- The audit **observes** an already-computed `ProviderRenderOutcome` and maps it: `rendered → validation-passed`; `failed`+`provider-output-failed-validation` → `validation-failed` (with the underlying `RenderingFailure[]`); `failed`+`unsupported-style`/`unsupported-locale`/`unsafe-provider-request` → `unsafe-request-blocked`; other `ProviderFailure` → `provider-failed`.
- **No raw draft retention:** `ProviderDraftSummary` is reason/count-based (`draftProduced`, `providerWarningCount?`, `validationFailureCount?`, `renderingFailureReasons?`, `providerFailureReason?`); **`rawDraftRetained` is the literal `false`**; reconstitution **rejects** any `draft`/`text`/`content`/`prompt` key or `rawDraftRetained: true`, and rejects unknown (payload-bag) keys + status/flag mismatches.
- **Observe-only:** `auditProviderAttempt` is a **pure mapping** — it **does not call** `requestProviderRendering` / `ProviderAdapter` / `validateDraft`. It records refs (renderable/source ref, terminal-output kind, domain `VoiceMode`), the provider adapter kind, the status, the reasons, and a safe draft summary.
- **Auditability, not authority:** a `ProviderAttemptRecord` is **not** a `ProviderDraft` / source truth / `Evidence` / `Observation` / `Understanding` / `AthleteDecision` / `DecisionSupport` / `TerminalOutput` / `RenderedMessage` / `RenderedMessageRecord`; it **creates no review/display-eligibility/delivery**, **appends no event**, **triggers no retry/scheduler/reprojection/reasoning**, and **mutates nothing**. A **validation failure is not domain invalidation**; provider success is not recommendation validation; provider failure does not weaken `SupportQuality`.
- The repository uses the Impl 010 pattern (deep-copy round-trip; mutation isolation; validated reconstitution); the audit imports only its own `rendering` surfaces + read-only `decision-support` *types*; **no module outside `rendering` imports it**; **no `event-recording` import / event-catalog expansion**.
- **Still absent (intentional):** a real provider/SDK + production prompts; provider/delivery event records; provider telemetry / model evaluation; UI/API; a scheduler/retry layer; a production DB.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **provider attempt record ≠ provider draft ≠ source truth** · **≠ `Evidence`/`Observation`/`Understanding`/`AthleteDecision`/`DecisionSupport`/`TerminalOutput`**.
- **provider attempt record ≠ `RenderedMessage`/`RenderedMessageRecord`** · **audit ≠ rendered-message persistence/review/display-eligibility/delivery/event record**.
- **audit observes outcome ≠ audit calls provider/validator** · **validation failure ≠ domain invalidation** · **provider success ≠ recommendation validation** · **provider failure ≠ support-quality weakening**.
- **provider attempt audit ≠ model evaluation / telemetry infrastructure** · **no raw draft retention ≠ no auditability**.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora can now remember what the provider seam did — a safe-summary, append-only `ProviderAttemptRecord` (status + real-catalog reasons, no raw draft) — by observing the outcome, never calling the provider/validator; the record is auditability not authority, retains no draft, triggers nothing downstream, and validated messages remain the only path to a `RenderedMessage`.**

---

## Update — Implementation 019 (Real-Provider-Ready Boundary)

[FACT] **Implementation 019** opened the most dangerous edge safely: it made a **real provider pluggable** behind the existing seam — accepting the *shapes* of secrets, network, prompt material, and provider errors — **without touching a real provider** and **without changing the authority model**. A real provider changes the **draft source**, not the gate. It is **additive**: only the two `rendering` index files changed (additive exports); the **synchronous Impl 017 seam is untouched**; **no new top-level module**, **no documented blocker**.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- `rendering` gained (in `domain/` + `application/`): `ProviderSecretRef` (+ `ProviderCredentialStatus`), a non-secret `ProviderClientConfig`, a structured `ProviderInstruction` (+ `providerInstructionFrom`), `ProviderClientRequest`/`ProviderClientResponse` (+ operational `ProviderClientMetadata`), a closed **`ProviderOperationalFailure`** (+ `toProviderFailure`), an **async `ProviderClientBoundary`** port, a deterministic **`FakeProviderClient`**, a **`RealProviderAdapter`**, and an async **`requestRealProviderRendering`** service.
- **Option B (additive async; sync seam untouched):** the existing synchronous `ProviderAdapter`/`FakeProviderAdapter`/`requestProviderRendering` (Impl 017) are **unchanged**; the new async path coexists. This is the **first `async`/`Promise` surface** in the codebase, isolated to the real-ready path.
- The async flow **reuses** the unchanged `providerRenderingRequestFrom` guard (unsafe requests refused **before** any client call), adds a **credential fast-path** (a non-`present` `ProviderSecretRef` fails safely before the call), calls the async client for an **untrusted draft**, then runs the **unchanged mandatory `validateDraft`**, and returns the **existing `ProviderRenderOutcome`** (validation failure → `provider-output-failed-validation` + the underlying `RenderingFailure[]`).
- **Secret refs, never secrets:** `ProviderSecretRef` is a status (`present`/`missing`/`invalid`) + an opaque ref; **no raw secret** in records/responses/errors, **no `process.env`**, none audited.
- **Structured instruction, not prompts:** `ProviderInstruction` is **derived** from the constrained request (kind, voice, allowed/forbidden claims, uncertainty/limitation/traceability constraints, safe style/locale); **no prompt-template file, no arbitrary prompt text, no chain-of-thought**.
- **Failure mapping, no expansion:** `ProviderOperationalFailure` (missing/invalid credential, unavailable, timeout, rate-limit, refused, empty, malformed, unsupported-config, unsafe-request) maps **down** to the **existing** `ProviderFailure` via `toProviderFailure`; the core catalog is **not expanded**. Every failure **degrades to safe non-rendering** with **no automatic retry**.
- **Auditability preserved, not automated:** the Impl 018 raw-free audit can observe the real outcome by **explicit composition**; the service **persists nothing automatically**. **Provider metadata is operational, not evidence.**
- **Still absent (intentional):** a real provider/SDK + production prompts + a real secret mechanism / network; provider/delivery event records; provider telemetry / model evaluation; UI/API; a scheduler/retry layer; a production DB.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **real-provider-ready boundary ≠ real provider integration** · **fake client ≠ real SDK/network** · **secret ref ≠ secret** · **provider instruction ≠ arbitrary prompt / production prompt template**.
- **async client boundary ≠ automatic retry/scheduler** · **failure mapping ≠ expanding provider authority** · **provider operational metadata ≠ evidence**.
- **provider draft ≠ rendered message** · **sync seam untouched ≠ duplicated authority** · **`ProviderRenderOutcome` ≠ provider-attempt persistence** · **real-provider-ready path ≠ delivery/eventing**.
- **provider success ≠ recommendation validation** · **provider failure ≠ domain invalidation**.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora is now real-provider-*ready* — a real provider is pluggable behind an additive async client boundary (proven with a deterministic fake in-process client; operational secret refs, structured instructions, failure mapping) that still ends at the unchanged mandatory `validateDraft` and returns the existing outcome; the sync seam is untouched, secrets/metadata stay operational, the audit stays raw-free, and nothing real (SDK/network/secret/prompt) is touched and no downstream side effect occurs.**

---

## Update — Implementation 020 (Concrete-Provider Adapter Shell)

[FACT] **Implementation 020** added the **first selected-provider adapter shell** behind the Impl 019 async `ProviderClientBoundary` — a concrete adapter that proves vendor-specific **serialization / parsing / error-mapping** against deterministic fixtures **without touching a real provider**. The provider target (**OpenAI**) was selected at the **doc/decision level only** (Tech Spec 020A); production/test code stays **vendor-neutral** (`concrete-provider-*`) so **no negative-capability guard was weakened and no vendor token leaks into a guarded file**. It is **additive**: only the `rendering/application/index.ts` export surface changed; **no new top-level module**, **no package/lockfile change**, **no documented blocker**.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- `rendering/application/` gained: a **`ConcreteProviderClient`** (implements the async `ProviderClientBoundary`), a pure **`serializeProviderInstruction`** (+ `ConcreteProviderRequestPayload`), a pure **`parseProviderResponse`** (+ `ConcreteProviderResponseShape`), and a pure **`mapProviderError`** (+ `ConcreteProviderErrorKind`/`ConcreteProviderErrorShape`). All four files live **inside `rendering/application`**.
- **Provider selected at decision level, neutral in code:** 020A records **OpenAI** as the first concrete-provider target; the code uses neutral `concrete-provider-*` names and a neutral `providerKind` (`"concrete"`). The vendor token never appears in a guarded provider file.
- **Disabled by default, fails safe:** with no injected transport, `ConcreteProviderClient.requestDraft` returns a safe failure (`provider-unavailable`) and does **no work** — **no live call path exists**. A non-`present` credential fails safe (`missing-credential`/`invalid-credential`) **before** any transport is consulted. The only non-default behavior is a **deterministic in-process fixture transport** used **only by tests** (not a network call).
- **Serializer is structured and safe:** `serializeProviderInstruction` is a pure projection of `ProviderInstruction` into a neutral provider-shaped payload carrying **only** safe constraints (terminal-output kind, voice, style, locale, allowed/forbidden claims, uncertainty-visible requirement, limitations, traceability, maxLength). There is **no field** for an arbitrary prompt / chain-of-thought / hidden reasoning / voice override / secret — they are unrepresentable; **no prompt-template file, no `src/prompts`**.
- **Parser returns untrusted draft + operational metadata only:** `parseProviderResponse` extracts only draft text (untrusted) + operational metadata (provider kind / finish reason / token count / latency); empty → `provider-returned-empty-response`, malformed → `provider-returned-malformed-response`; it retains **no raw provider payload** and **never** creates a `RenderedMessage`.
- **Error mapper maps down, no expansion:** `mapProviderError` maps provider-shaped errors (live-disabled, missing/invalid credential, network-unavailable, timeout, rate-limit, refusal, empty, malformed, unsupported-config, unknown) to the existing **`ProviderOperationalFailure`**, which the existing `toProviderFailure` maps **down** to the existing **`ProviderFailure`** (**not expanded**); an unknown error fails safe (`provider-unavailable`) and leaks no raw payload/secret.
- **Validator + audit unchanged:** a concrete-client draft becomes a `RenderedMessage` **only** via the unchanged `requestRealProviderRendering` → **`validateDraft`**; the Impl 018 raw-free audit observes the outcome by **explicit composition** (no automatic persistence; `rawDraftRetained` literal `false`).
- **No new dependency / network / secret / side effect:** **no SDK installed** (`package.json`/`package-lock.json` unchanged; a test asserts devDeps remain `typescript` + `@types/node`); **no network, no `process.env`, no raw secret, no retry/scheduler/event bus**; **no record/review/display-eligibility/delivery/event/domain mutation**.
- **Still absent (intentional):** a **live provider call** (the shell is disabled by default; live calls are a later slice), a real SDK/secret-mechanism/network, production prompts, provider/delivery event records, provider telemetry / model evaluation, UI/API, a scheduler/retry layer, and a production DB.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **provider target selected ≠ live provider integration** · **vendor doc decision ≠ vendor token in production code** · **concrete-provider shell ≠ SDK client**.
- **disabled-by-default client ≠ live-call adapter** · **fixture transport ≠ network** · **secret ref ≠ raw secret**.
- **serializer ≠ arbitrary prompt** · **serializer ≠ production prompt template** · **parser output ≠ rendered message** · **provider metadata ≠ evidence**.
- **provider-shaped error ≠ domain invalidation** · **`ProviderOperationalFailure` mapping ≠ expanding `ProviderFailure`** · **provider success ≠ persistence/review/delivery** · **composed audit ≠ automatic audit persistence**.
- **no SDK dependency ≠ no provider plan** · **selected-provider shell ≠ weakening negative-capability guards**.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora now has the first selected-provider adapter shell behind the async client boundary — OpenAI chosen at the doc/decision level while code stays vendor-neutral (`concrete-provider-*`), a disabled-by-default client plus deterministic serializer/parser/error-mapper — adding no SDK, no network, no live call, no API keys, no env reads, no raw secrets, no prompt templates, no automatic persistence, no review/display/delivery/event side effect, and no domain mutation; provider output stays untrusted and must pass `validateDraft`. This is a selected-provider *shell*, not live provider integration.**

---

## Update — Implementation 021 (Opt-In Live-Provider Boundary)

[FACT] **Implementation 021** opened the **first live-call edge** — and kept it **fail-closed**: a provider call can now be *real* network I/O, but only behind the existing async `ProviderClientBoundary`, only under explicit opt-in, and only through **native `fetch` isolated in a single approved transport file**. **No SDK was installed, no dependency/lockfile changed, no environment variable is read, no real secret mechanism exists, and the default test suite / CI make no live call and require no credentials.** A live call is **operational I/O; it does not change the authority model** — `validateDraft` stays the gate, the audit stays raw-free, provider output stays untrusted. It is **additive**: only the `rendering/application/index.ts` exports and **two rendering network guards** changed (surgically); **no new module**, **no documented blocker**.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- `rendering/application/` gained: a **`LiveCallPolicy`** (injected value object; `disabled()` / `enabled({timeoutMs})`), a **`ProviderCredentialResolver`** port (+ opaque `ProviderCredentialToken`), a deterministic **`StaticProviderCredentialResolver`** (test/composition only), a **`LiveProviderHttpTransport`** (the only network-token file), and a **`LiveProviderClient`** (implements the async `ProviderClientBoundary`).
- **Disabled by default, fail-closed:** `LiveCallPolicy.disabled()` is the safe default; opt-in is **explicit** via the injected policy (never inferred from the environment; no global state). The client **fails closed before any transport call** when the policy is disabled, or the credential is missing/invalid (→ safe `provider-unavailable` / `missing-credential` / `invalid-credential`).
- **Native HTTP, isolated, no SDK:** `LiveProviderHttpTransport` is the **only** production file permitted a network token (`fetch` + `AbortSignal.timeout`, behind an **injected endpoint** — no hard-coded vendor URL). **No SDK installed; `package.json`/`package-lock.json` unchanged.** The transport does no retry, no persistence, no validation, no domain mutation, and leaks no secret in errors.
- **Credentials never become domain data:** the credential resolver is **injected**; the static resolver is deterministic/test-only with a **non-secret sentinel**; **no env resolver exists and no `process.env` is read**; the credential is used transiently in the request header only — never persisted/audited/logged/in errors.
- **`LiveProviderClient` is a sibling of `ConcreteProviderClient`** (async network transport vs sync fixture), **reusing** the unchanged `serializeProviderInstruction` / `parseProviderResponse` / `mapProviderError`. It **never calls `validateDraft`** — validation stays owned by `requestRealProviderRendering(...)`; provider output is an **untrusted draft**.
- **Failure mapping, no expansion:** transport conditions (live-disabled, missing/invalid credential, timeout, rate-limit, network-unavailable, refusal, empty, malformed, unsupported-config, unknown) map onto the **existing** `ProviderOperationalFailure → ProviderFailure` — **neither catalog expanded**; unknown fails safe (`provider-unavailable`) leaking nothing.
- **Audit raw-free, nothing automatic:** a live attempt is observed by the Impl 018 `auditProviderAttempt` only by **explicit composition** (no automatic persistence; `rawDraftRetained` literal `false`); there is **no record/review/display-eligibility/delivery/event/domain-mutation** side effect and **no retry/scheduler/event bus**.
- **Surgical guard exception:** the Impl 014 broad rendering scan and the Impl 017 `/provider-/` scan now allow a network token **only** in `live-provider-http-transport.ts` (each with a positive "exactly one network file" assertion); **vendor / SDK / env tokens stay forbidden everywhere**, including that file. The Impl 019/020 guards were **not touched**.
- **Untouched:** the synchronous provider seam, `FakeProviderAdapter`, `FakeProviderClient`, and `ConcreteProviderClient`.
- **Still absent (intentional):** a **production secret/env resolver** (env reads deferred), a real SDK, **production live-call rollout** (the boundary is *capable*, not *deployed*), production prompts, provider/delivery event records, telemetry / model evaluation, UI/API, a scheduler/retry layer, a production DB.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **live-provider boundary ≠ production rollout** · **opt-in capability ≠ enabled-by-default live call** · **native HTTP transport ≠ SDK dependency** · **one approved network file ≠ broad network permission**.
- **credential resolver port ≠ real secret manager** · **static resolver ≠ production credential mechanism** · **injected credential token ≠ persisted secret** · **fetch exception ≠ weakened vendor/env/SDK guards**.
- **disabled policy ≠ transport invocation** · **missing credential ≠ transport invocation** · **invalid credential ≠ domain failure**.
- **provider payload ≠ arbitrary prompt** · **transport response ≠ rendered message** · **parsed draft ≠ validated message** · **provider metadata ≠ evidence** · **transport failure ≠ domain invalidation**.
- **composed audit ≠ automatic audit persistence** · **live-capable client ≠ retry/scheduler/event bus** · **live-provider success ≠ persistence/review/display/delivery**.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora can now make a *real* provider call — but only when explicitly enabled, behind the unchanged `ProviderClientBoundary` and the unchanged `validateDraft`, with native `fetch` sealed in one approved file, credentials injected (never env-read, never persisted), the audit raw-free, and the default suite/CI credential-free and non-live. A live call is operational I/O; it changes the draft source, never the authority model. This is a live-call-*capable* boundary, not a production live-provider rollout.**

---

## Update — Implementation 022 (Injected Environment Credential Resolver)

[FACT] **Implementation 022** supplied the first credential resolver that reads from an environment/config **source** — behind the **unchanged injected `ProviderCredentialResolver` port** — **without reading the real process environment**. It reads from an **injected, read-only source map** (a deterministic map in tests; a future infra slice may snapshot the real environment into it), so it adds the next "real outside world" capability (credential resolution) while keeping `process.env` **forbidden everywhere** and requiring **no structural-guard exception**. A credential is **operational**, not domain data; **availability is not live-call enablement**. It is **additive**: only the `rendering/application/index.ts` exports changed; **no guard change**, **no dependency change**, **no documented blocker**.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- `rendering/application/` gained an **`EnvironmentProviderCredentialResolver`** (+ `EnvironmentCredentialSource`, `EnvironmentResolverConfig`, `CredentialValidationPolicy`) — a **sibling** of `StaticProviderCredentialResolver` on the same port.
- **Injected source, not the real environment:** it takes an injected `EnvironmentCredentialSource` (`Readonly<Record<string, string | undefined>>`) and reads **exactly one explicitly configured key** — **no `process.env`**, **no scan**, **no fallback list**, **no domain-derived key name**.
- **Deterministic classification:** absent key → `missing`; blank/whitespace value → `invalid`; control characters / line breaks → `invalid`; too-short value → `invalid`; otherwise → `available` with the existing **opaque transient `ProviderCredentialToken`**. A blank/whitespace **key name** fails closed (`invalid`).
- **Secret stays transient:** the raw credential never appears in failures, the provider-client outcome, the raw-free audit, persisted state, provider metadata, or tests; failures use the existing `missing`/`invalid` states (stable, non-secret).
- **Availability ≠ live-call enablement:** composed into a `LiveProviderClient`, a `LiveCallPolicy.disabled()` still prevents the transport, and a missing/invalid credential prevents the transport even when the policy is enabled. The resolver **calls no transport / provider / `validateDraft`**, persists nothing, audits nothing, mutates no domain.
- **No expansion, nothing automatic:** `ProviderFailure` / `ProviderOperationalFailure` are **not expanded**; the Impl 018 audit stays raw-free by explicit composition; there is **no record/review/display-eligibility/delivery/event/domain-mutation** side effect and **no retry/scheduler**.
- **No env token, no guard exception:** `process.env` appears **nowhere** in `src/` (verified); the resolver file is already scanned by the Impl 017 `/provider-/` and Impl 021 `/provider-credential/` guards (both forbid `process.env`), plus a new `environment-secret-negative-capability.test.ts` — **no guard was weakened**.
- **Untouched:** the static resolver, the live transport, the concrete-provider shell, the sync seam, `FakeProviderAdapter`, and `FakeProviderClient`.
- **Still absent (intentional):** a **direct `process.env` adapter** (deferred to a future infra slice that snapshots the environment into the injected map), a **production secret manager**, real credentials in CI/tests, a production live-call rollout, provider/delivery events, telemetry / model evaluation, UI/API, a scheduler/retry layer, a production DB.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **injected env source ≠ real process environment** · **environment-like resolver ≠ production secret manager** · **configured key lookup ≠ environment scan**.
- **available credential ≠ live-call enablement** · **credential resolver ≠ transport invocation / provider call / validation** · **opaque token ≠ persisted secret**.
- **credential failure ≠ domain failure** · **secret absence ≠ support-quality downgrade** · **raw credential ≠ provider metadata / audit payload / traceability evidence**.
- **resolver boundary ≠ infrastructure module** · **no `process.env` token ≠ no future production secret plan** · **injected tests ≠ CI credential requirement**.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora can now resolve a provider credential from an injected environment/config source behind the unchanged `ProviderCredentialResolver` port — reading one configured key, returning the existing resolution states with an opaque transient token — without reading the real `process.env`, requiring a real credential in CI/tests, adding a dependency or a guard exception, enabling live calls by itself, leaking a raw secret, or producing any persistence/review/delivery/event/domain side effect. It is an injected *operational* resolver, not a production secret manager.**

---

## Update — Implementation 023 (One-File Process-Environment Source Adapter)

[FACT] **Implementation 023** bound credential resolution to the **real process environment** — through **exactly one approved adapter file** — without turning `process.env` into an open door. A `ProcessEnvironmentCredentialSourceAdapter` reads **one configured key** (via an injected accessor) and produces the existing injected `EnvironmentCredentialSource` shape (Impl 022) — it **feeds, does not replace,** the resolver. The **direct `process.env` token now appears in exactly one production file** (`process-environment-credential-source-adapter.ts`), enforced by a **new repo-wide guard**; everywhere else it stays absent. It is **additive**: only the `rendering/application/index.ts` exports and the new guard test were added; **no existing guard was weakened**, **no dependency changed**, **no documented blocker**.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- `rendering/application/` gained a **`ProcessEnvironmentCredentialSourceAdapter`** (+ `ProcessEnvironmentAccessor`, `processEnvironmentCredentialSourceAdapter(keyName?)` factory, `defaultProcessEnvironmentAccessor`, `APPROVED_PROVIDER_CREDENTIAL_KEY`).
- **Feeds the resolver, does not replace it:** `toEnvironmentCredentialSource()` reads **exactly one explicitly configured key** (the accessor is called **once**), returns a source containing **only** that key when a value is present, else an **empty source** — and **classifies nothing** (a blank/whitespace value passes through; a blank/whitespace key name **fails closed** to an empty source). `EnvironmentProviderCredentialResolver` still does all classification.
- **`process.env` sealed to one file:** the adapter **requires an injected `ProcessEnvironmentAccessor`** (no implicit default), so tests inject a fake and **never read the real environment**; `defaultProcessEnvironmentAccessor` — the **only** direct `process.env` read site in the codebase — is wired only by the production factory and is **never used by the default suite**. The approved key is **neutral** (`AURORA_PROVIDER_CREDENTIAL`).
- **A new repo-wide guard** scans all production `src/` files and asserts the `process.env` token appears in **exactly** the approved adapter file (the guard builds the token regex indirectly so the test is not itself a token site). **No existing provider/network/vendor/SDK/prompt guard was touched**; the network token stays confined to the Impl 021 transport file.
- **Availability ≠ live-call enablement, secret stays transient:** a `LiveCallPolicy.disabled()` and a missing/invalid credential each still block the transport; the raw secret never appears in the adapter's errors/results, the provider-client outcome, or the raw-free audit. The adapter **calls no resolver (unless the caller composes it) / live client / transport / provider / `validateDraft`**, persists/audits/logs nothing, mutates no domain, and **expands no failure catalog**.
- **No dependency / no real env in tests / nothing automatic:** `package.json`/`package-lock.json` unchanged; the default suite/CI need **no real environment value and make no live call**; there is **no record/review/display-eligibility/delivery/event/domain-mutation** side effect and **no retry/scheduler**.
- **Untouched:** `EnvironmentProviderCredentialResolver` (still the classifier), `StaticProviderCredentialResolver`, the live transport, the concrete shell, the sync seam, `FakeProviderAdapter`, and `FakeProviderClient`.
- **Still absent (intentional):** a **production secret manager**, secret rotation, a production live-call rollout, real credentials in CI/tests, provider/delivery events, telemetry / model evaluation, UI/API, a scheduler/retry layer, a production DB.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **process-env adapter ≠ secret manager** · **direct process-environment binding ≠ broad environment access** · **one-file token confinement ≠ guard weakening** · **process-environment token exception ≠ guard weakening** (none was excepted — a stronger repo-wide guard was *added*).
- **default accessor ≠ default test behavior** · **fake-accessor tests ≠ production secret wiring** · **production factory ≠ live call enabled by default**.
- **adapter output ≠ credential classification** · **adapter ≠ resolver** · **resolver classification ≠ live-call enablement** · **available environment value ≠ provider call / transport invocation**.
- **raw environment value ≠ domain data / audit payload / provider metadata** · **process-env adapter ≠ `validateDraft`** · **process-env adapter ≠ persistence/review/display/delivery/event**.

[ASSUMPTION] The headline: **Aurora can now bind the injected credential resolver to the real process environment through exactly one approved adapter — reading one neutral key via an injected accessor, feeding (not replacing) the resolver — with `process.env` sealed to that one file by a new repo-wide guard, no real environment value required in tests/CI, no dependency or existing-guard change, no live-call enablement by itself, no raw-secret leakage, and no persistence/review/delivery/event/domain side effect. It is a one-file *operational* source adapter, not a production secret manager.**

---

## Update — Implementation 024 (Provider / Rendering / Delivery Event Surface)

[FACT] **Implementation 024** closed the **occurrence-history gap** at the output-out edge: `event-recording` can now record that a provider attempt, a rendered-message record, a render review, a display-eligibility derivation, a delivery request, or a delivery outcome **happened** — as **append-only, ref-only `DomainEventRecord`s**. This is an **additive catalog expansion + pure factories**, not an event bus: catalogs gained string-literal members and `event-recording/application` gained pure functions that **return** records and **persist nothing**. **Events record what happened; they do not make anything happen.** It is **additive and dependency-neutral**: `event-recording` still imports only `shared-kernel`, and **no rendering/delivery/provider path imports `event-recording` or auto-emits**. The only existing-file changes are the three additive catalog edits, the `event-recording/application/index.ts` exports, and a **reconciliation** of two earlier "catalog not yet extended" guards (Impl 015/018) that this approved slice supersedes; **no production behavior changed, no dependency changed, no documented blocker**.

[FACT] **Now true:**
- **Additive catalogs (every prior entry intact):** `ProducingModule` += `rendering`, `delivery` (the `isProducingModule` predicate recognizes them); `EventArtifactKind` += `ProviderAttemptRecord`, `RenderedMessageRecord`, `RenderReview`, `DeliveryRequest`, `DeliveryRecord`; `DomainEventType` += eight occurrence/outcome types — `ProviderAttemptRecorded`, `ProviderDraftValidationFailed`, `ProviderDraftValidationPassed`, `RenderedMessageRecorded`, `RenderReviewRecorded`, `DisplayEligibilityDerived` (all module `rendering`), `DeliveryRequestRecorded`, `DeliveryOutcomeRecorded` (module `delivery`) — each with its `DOMAIN_EVENT_CATALOG` entry.
- **Provider events are produced by `rendering`** (the provider edge lives inside `rendering`); **no `provider` producing module was added.** Delivery events are produced by `delivery`.
- **`DisplayEligibility` is NOT an artifact kind** — it is id-less (a derived value), so it is carried as a **safe `role`** (`display-eligible`/`display-ineligible`) on the `RenderedMessageRecord` ref, never forced into a kind.
- **Eight pure factories** in `event-recording/application/provider-rendering-delivery-events.ts` build each event through the **existing `DomainEventRecord.record(...)`**. They **persist nothing**, **call no provider / live transport / validator / renderer / delivery sink**, **create no rendered-message record / review / delivery record / provider attempt**, **mutate no domain state**, and have **no side effect** — recording is **explicit application composition only**.
- **Payloads stay ref-only and raw-free:** every ref carries only `kind`/`id`/`role?`/`ownerModule?` (the existing `EventPayloadRef` discipline). **No raw draft/prompt/payload/provider-response/secret/env value/chain-of-thought/copied body/metadata bag is representable**; a serialized-state scan proves no `bearer`/`authorization`/`process.env`/`apikey`/`secret`/`prompt`/`draft` marker leaks.
- **Dependency-neutral, no auto-emit:** `event-recording` imports **only `shared-kernel`** (the factory file imports its own domain + `shared-kernel`); **rendering/delivery/provider paths import no `event-recording` and emit nothing automatically**; appending/reading a record **executes nothing**.
- **Guard reconciliation, not weakening:** the Impl 015/018 guards that asserted "the event catalog was not extended" were updated for the approved expansion. The **stronger** post-024 invariant: `event-recording` may contain the approved ref-kind/event-type **strings**, but still **imports nothing from rendering/delivery/provider**, the **rendering-internal audit symbols (`auditProviderAttempt`, the audit repository) remain forbidden outside `rendering`**, and the factories remain **pure and side-effect-free**.
- **Still absent (intentional):** an **event bus / publish-subscribe / handler / async delivery**, a **queue / scheduler / retry mechanism**, **auto-emission** from any rendering/delivery/provider operation, **automatic persistence** of events, a **credential-resolution event** (deferred), **telemetry / model evaluation**, a **production DB / schema / migration**, and any **live call / SDK / dependency** change.

[FACT] **Distinctions this update makes explicit** (do not collapse):
- **event catalog expansion ≠ event bus** · **event factory ≠ event persistence** · **event record ≠ command / retry trigger / delivery trigger**.
- **event record ≠ evidence / quality judgment / domain mutation** · **provider success event ≠ recommendation correctness** · **delivery success event ≠ athlete saw/understood/accepted**.
- **provider attempt event ≠ provider attempt audit** · **provider validation event ≠ validator execution** · **rendered-message event ≠ rendered-message creation** · **review event ≠ display command** · **display-eligibility event ≠ delivery command** · **delivery request event ≠ delivery send** · **delivery outcome event ≠ athlete reception/decision**.
- **ref-only event payload ≠ copied state / raw content store** · **event-recording vocabulary string ≠ cross-module import** · **event history read ≠ replay side effect** · **guard reconciliation ≠ boundary weakening**.
